44015012	The whole assembly remained silent and listened to Barnabas and Paul relating all the signs and wonders that God had done through them among the Gentiles .
44015013	When they ceased speaking , James said , " Brethren , listen to me .
44015014	Symeon has told how first God graciously visited the Gentiles and took a people for his name .
44015015	With this the words of the prophets agree , as it is written ,
44015016	' After this I will return and build up again the tent of David which has fallen down ; yes , I will build up its ruins and erect it again ,
44015017	that the rest of mankind may seek the Lord , even all the Gentiles upon whom my name has been bestowed , says the Lord
44015018	who does these things foreknown from of old . '
44015019	Therefore I judge best not to trouble those of the Gentiles who have turned to God ,
44015020	but to write to them to abstain from contamination with idols , and from unchastity , and from what has been strangled , and from blood .
44015021	For Moses has had for generations past in every city those who preach him , for he is read in the synagogues every Sabbath . "
44015022	Then it seemed good to the apostles and the elders , with the whole church , to select men from themselves and to send them to Antioch with Paul and Barnabas ; namely , Judas called Barsabbas , and Silas , men esteemed among the brethren .
44015023	They wrote and sent by their hands the following letter : " The Apostles and the Brethren who are elders , to the Brethren from the Gentiles in Antioch and Syria and Cilicia : Greeting .
44015024	" Inasmuch as we have heard that certain persons from us have troubled you with words , unsettling your minds , â men whom we did not authorize , â
44015025	it seemed good , after unanimous agreement , to select some men and send them to you with our beloved Barnabas and Paul ,
44015026	who have exposed their lives for the name of our Lord Jesus Christ .
44015027	We have sent therefore Judas and Silas , who will tell you orally the same things .
44015028	For it seemed good to the Holy Spirit and to us to lay on you no further burden than these necessary things :
44015029	to abstain from things sacrificed to idols , and from blood , and from strangled things , and from unchastity . If you keep yourselves from these you will do well . Farewell . "
44015030	So they were sent away and went down to Antioch , where they called together the whole body and delivered over the letter .
44015031	On reading it they rejoiced over the encouragement .
44015032	Both Judas and Silas , being themselves prophets , encouraged and confirmed the brethren by long addresses .
44015033	After spending some time they were sent away with a message of peace from the brethren to those who had sent them .
44015035	Paul and Barnabas stayed on in Antioch teaching and telling , in association with many others , the good news of the Lord's message .
44015036	After some time Paul said to Barnabas , " Let us go back and visit the brethren in every city in which we made known the Lord's message , and see how they are prospering . "
44015037	Barnabas wished to take along John who was called Mark .
44015038	But Paul did not approve of taking him along , since he had left them in Pamphylia and had not gone on with them into the work .
44015039	Such a difference of feeling resulted that they separated from each other . Barnabas took Mark and sailed away to Cyprus .
44015040	Paul selected Silas and left , after being commended to the grace of the Lord by the brethren .
44015041	They went through Syria and Cilicia strengthening the churches .
44016001	THEY came to Derbe and Lystra . At Lystra there was a disciple named Timothy , the son of a Jewish woman , who was a believer , and of a Greek father .
44016002	He had a good reputation among the brethren in Lystra and Iconium .
44016003	Paul wished to have Timothy go with him . So he took him and circumcised him because of the Jews who were in those parts . For they all knew that his father was a Greek .
44016004	Thus they traveled through the cities and delivered to the disciples for observance the rules that had been decided on by the apostles and elders in Jerusalem .
44016005	So the churches grew firmer in faith and increased in numbers from day to day .
44016006	They went through Phrygia and the Galatian country , the Holy Spirit having prevented their speaking the message in Asia .
44016007	Upon reaching Mysia they attempted to go into Bithynia , but the spirit of Jesus did not allow them .
44016008	Passing by Mysia they came down to Troas .
44016009	There a vision appeared to Paul in the night â a Macedonian man was standing and begging him saying , " Come over into Macedonia and help us . "
44016010	After Paul had seen the vision , we at once tried to go out to Macedonia , inferring that God had called on us to tell the good news to the people there .
44016011	Sailing away from Troas we made a straight run to Samothrace , and on the next day to Neapolis .
44016012	From there we went to Philippi , which is the first city of that part of Macedonia and is a Roman colony . We remained in that city for a number of days .
44016013	On the Sabbath day we went outside of the gate to a place on the riverside where it was customary to go for prayer , and we sat down and talked with the women who had gathered there .
44016014	One woman named Lydia , a dealer in purple , from the city of Thyatira , who reverenced God , was listening . God opened her heart to receive what was said by Paul .
44016015	When she had been baptized along with her household , she begged us , " If you have judged me to be faithful to the Lord , come into my house and stay , " and she insisted on our doing so .
44016016	It so happened that as we were going to the place of prayer a certain slave girl who had a spirit of divination met us . She was bringing great gain to her masters by divining .
44016017	She followed Paul and us and kept calling out , " These men are servants of God Most High , and they are teaching you the way of salvation . "
44016018	This she kept doing for many days . Paul was annoyed , and turning he said to the spirit , " I tell you in the name of Jesus Christ to come out of her , " and it came out at that very moment .
44016019	When her masters saw that the hope of their gain was gone , they laid hold of Paul and Silas and dragged them into the public square before the authorities .
44016020	Bringing them in , they said to the magistrates , " These men , who are Jews , are disturbing our city
44016021	and teaching customs which it is not proper for us , who are Romans , to receive or practice . "
44016022	The crowd joined in the attack upon them , and the magistrates tore off their clothes and ordered them to be beaten with rods .
44016023	After laying many stripes upon them they cast them into prison , ordering the jailer to keep them securely .
44016024	He on receiving such an order thrust them into the inner prison and made their feet secure in the stocks .
44016025	But about midnight Paul and Silas were praying and singing hymns to God , and the other prisoners were listening .
44016026	Suddenly there was a great earthquake , so that the foundations of the prison were shaken . Immediately all the doors were opened and every one's fetters were loosed .
44016027	The jailer , waking from sleep and seeing the doors of the prison open , drew his sword and was about to kill himself , thinking that the prisoners had escaped .
44016028	But Paul said with a loud voice , " Do no harm to yourself , for we are all here . "
44016029	Calling for a light he sprang in and fell down trembling before Paul and Silas ,
44016030	and led them out and said , " Men , what must I do to be saved ? "
44016031	They said , " Believe in the Lord Jesus and you will be saved , and your household , "
44016032	and they told the message of God to him and to all who were in his house .
44016033	He took them at that hour of the night and washed their stripes . Then he was baptized , he and all of his household , immediately .
44016034	He brought them into his house and spread the table for them , and rejoiced with his whole family because he had believed in God .
44016035	When morning came the magistrates sent their orderlies to say , " Set those men at liberty . "
44016036	The jailer told this order to Paul , " The magistrates have sent to have you set at liberty . Now go out and proceed on your journey in peace . "
44016037	But Paul said to them , " After beating us publicly and without a trial , although we are Romans , they cast us into prison . And are they now sending us out secretly ? No , let them come themselves and lead us out . "
44016038	The orderlies reported these words to the magistrates . When they heard that they were Romans they were alarmed ,
44016039	and came and begged them , and after leading them out requested them to leave the city .
44016040	They came out of the prison and went into Lydia's house , and after seeing and encouraging the brethren they departed .
44017001	AFTER passing through Amphipolis and Apollonia they came to Thessalonica . Here there was a synagogue of the Jews .
44017002	According to Paul's custom he went in to meet with them , and on three Sabbath days he reasoned with them from the Scriptures ,
44017003	explaining and showing that it was necessary that the Christ should suffer and rise from the dead , and saying , " Jesus of whom I am telling you is the Christ . "
44017004	Some of them were persuaded and attached themselves to Paul and Silas â a large number of the pious Greeks and not a few of the leading women .
44017005	But the Jews became excited and , taking with them some of the base loafers from the market-place , they made a mob and threw the city into confusion . They attacked the house of Jason and tried to bring Paul and Silas out to the people .
44017006	Not finding them , they dragged Jason and certain brethren before the magistrates , shouting , " These men who have upset the world have now come here .
44017007	Jason has received them . They all do contrary to the decrees of Caesar , saying that there is a different king â Jesus . "
44017008	Both the crowd and the magistrates were disturbed on hearing this .
44017009	So they took security from Jason and the rest and then dismissed them .
44017010	The brethren immediately sent off Paul and Silas in the night to Beraea . They on arrival went into the synagogue of the Jews .
44017011	These people were nobler than those in Thessalonica . They welcomed the message with all readiness and examined the Scriptures daily to see whether these things were so .
44017012	Consequently many of them believed , and also not a few Greeks ; women of high standing and men .
44017013	When the Jews of Thessalonica learned that God's message had been proclaimed by Paul also in Beraea , they came there agitating and disturbing the crowds .
44017014	At once then the brethren sent away Paul to go down to the sea coast . Silas and Timothy remained there .
44017015	Those who were conducting Paul took him as far as Athens , and , after receiving a letter to Silas and Timothy to come to him as soon as possible , they left .
44017016	While Paul was waiting for them in Athens , his spirit was stirred within him as he looked upon the city full of idols .
44017017	He often debated in the synagogue with the Jews and pious persons , and in the market-place every day with whoever happened to be there .
44017018	Some of the Epicurean and Stoic philosophers encountered him , and some said , " What can this idle talker mean ? " Others said , " He seems to be a proclaimer of foreign gods , " because he was telling the good news of Jesus and the resurrection .
44017019	They took him and led him up on to the Areopagus , saying , " May we know what this new doctrine that you are speaking of is ?
44017020	For you are bringing strange and surprising things to our ears . We wish to know what these things are . "
44017021	For all the Athenians and the foreigners residing there spent their time in nothing else than in telling or hearing something newer than the last .
44017022	Paul took his stand in the midst of the Areopagus and said : " Men of Athens , I see that you are in every way unusually reverential to the gods .
44017023	For in passing about and contemplating your sacred objects I came upon an altar on which was inscribed , ' To an unknown God . ' What you are worshiping in ignorance â that I am making known to you .
44017024	" The God who made the world and all the things that are in it , he who is Lord of heaven and earth , does not dwell in temples made by hands ,
44017025	nor is he served by human hands , as if he needed anything . For he gives to all life and breath and all things .
44017026	And he made of one every nation of men to dwell on all the face of the earth , having marked out the appointed times and the boundaries of their abodes ,
44017027	that they might seek for God , if they could feel after him and find him , though , indeed , he is not far from each one of us .
44017028	For in him we live and move and are ; as some of your own poets have said , ' For we also are his offspring . '
44017029	Being then the offspring of God , we ought not to think that deity is like gold or silver or stone , a thing carved by man's art and thought .
44017030	The times of ignorance God overlooked , but now he commands all men everywhere to change ,
44017031	since he has set a day in which he will soon judge the world in justice by the man whom he has appointed , and of whom he has given evidence to all men by raising him from the dead . "
44017032	When they heard of the resurrection of the dead , some sneered ; others said , " We will hear you again about this . "
44017033	So Paul went out from the midst of them .
44017034	But certain men attached themselves to him and believed . Among them was Dionysius the Areopagite , and there was a woman named Damaris and several other persons .
44018001	AFTER this Paul left Athens and came to Corinth .
44018002	There he found a Jew named Aquila , born in Pontus but recently come from Italy with Priscilla his wife , because Claudius had ordered all Jews to leave Rome . Paul visited these people ,
44018003	and because he was of the same trade stayed with them and they worked together ; for by trade they were tent-makers .
44018004	But in the synagogue every Sabbath he reasoned and endeavored to persuade both Jews and Greeks .
44018005	When Silas and Timothy came down from Macedonia , Paul was absorbed by the message , bearing witness to the Jews that Jesus was the Christ .
44018006	When they resisted and spoke profane words , he rent his garments and said to them , " Your blood is on your own heads . I am clear , and from now on I am going to the Gentiles . "
44018007	So he changed over from there and came into the house of a man named Titus Justus , who reverenced God . His house was next to the synagogue .
44018008	Crispus , the synagogue Director , believed in the Lord with all his household , and many of the Corinthians when they heard believed and were baptized .
44018009	The Lord spoke in the night by a vision to Paul , " Do not fear , but speak and be not silent ,
44018010	for I am with you and no one shall attack and harm you , for I have many people in this city . "
44018011	So he stayed a year and six months , teaching among them the message of God .
44018012	While Gallio was Proconsul of Achaia , the Jews with one mind made an attack on Paul and brought him before the court ,
44018013	saying , " This man is inducing men to worship God in a way contrary to law . "
44018014	As Paul was about to open his mouth , Gallio said to the Jews , " If it was some crime or wicked knavery , O you Jews , I would have reasonable patience with you .
44018015	But if it is a dispute about doctrine and names and your own law , see to it yourselves . I will not be a judge of these things , "
44018016	and he drove them from before the judge's seat .
44018017	Then they laid hold of Sosthenes , the synagogue Director , and beat him right in front of the judge's seat . But Gallio cared for none of these things .
44018018	Paul remained a number of days more . Then after taking leave of the brethren he sailed away to Syria , and Priscilla and Aquila went with him . He had shaved his head at Cenchreae , for he had a vow .
44018019	They came to Ephesus and Paul left his companions there . He himself went into the synagogue and debated with the Jews .
44018020	Although they begged him to stay longer , he did not consent ,
44018021	but took his leave , saying , " I will return to you again , God willing . "
44018022	From Ephesus he put to sea and came to Caesarea . Then he went up to Jerusalem and greeted the church , and from there returned to Antioch .
44018023	After spending some time there he set out and went through the Galatian country and Phrygia , place by place , strengthening all the disciples .
44018024	A certain Jew named Apollos , an Alexandrian by birth , a learned man , had come to Ephesus .
44018025	He was strong in knowledge of the Scriptures and had been instructed in the way of the Lord , and , being very earnest in spirit , was teaching accurately about Jesus , although he knew no baptism but John's .
44018026	This man began to speak fearlessly in the synagogue . When Priscilla and Aquila heard him , they took him and explained to him the way of God more accurately still .
44018027	As he wished to cross over to Achaia , the brethren encouraged him and wrote to the disciples to welcome him . So he went and greatly helped those who had believed through grace .
44018028	For he powerfully and publicly refuted the Jews , showing from the Scriptures that Jesus is the Christ .
44019001	WHILE Apollos was in Corinth , Paul , after passing through the upper country , came to Ephesus and found certain disciples .
44019002	He said to them , " Did you receive the Holy Spirit when you believed ? " They said to him , " On the contrary , we did not even hear that there was a Holy Spirit . "
44019003	He said , " How then were you baptized ? " They said , " With John's baptism . "
44019004	Paul said , " John baptized with the baptism of a change of heart , telling the people to believe in one who was coming after him , that is , in Jesus . "
44019005	On hearing that , they were baptized in the name of the Lord Jesus ,
44019006	and when Paul laid his hands on them the Holy Spirit came on them and they spoke with tongues and prophesied .
44019007	There were about twelve of these men in all .
44019008	For three months Paul went into the synagogue and spoke fearlessly , arguing persuasively regarding the kingdom of God .
44019009	When some were hardened and would not believe and spoke evil of the Way before the congregation , he departed from them and took away his disciples and discussed daily in the lecture-hall of Tyrannus .
44019010	This went on for two years , so that all the inhabitants of Asia , both Jews and Greeks , heard the message of the Lord .
44019011	Through the hands of Paul , God did miracles of no ordinary kind ,
44019012	so that handkerchiefs and aprons that had touched his body were carried to the sick , and the diseases left them and the evil spirits departed .
44019013	Then some of the wandering Jewish exorcists undertook to invoke over those who had evil spirits the name of the Lord Jesus , saying , " I adjure you by Jesus whom Paul proclaims . "
44019014	There were seven sons of a certain Sceva , a Jewish high priest , who did this .
44019015	But the evil spirit answered them , " Jesus I know and Paul I know ; but who are you ? "
44019016	and the man in whom the evil spirit was sprang on them and overpowered both of them , and so belabored them that they fled from that house naked and wounded .
44019017	This became known to all who were living in Ephesus , both Jews and Greeks , and awe fell on all of them , and the name of the Lord Jesus came to be held in high honor .
44019018	Many of those who had become believers came confessing and telling of their practices .
44019019	A number of those who had practiced magic brought their books and burned them before all . Adding up the prices of them they found the total to be fifty thousand pieces of silver .
44019020	Thus vigorously the Lord's message grew and strengthened .
44019021	When these things had been accomplished Paul took it in mind to pass through Macedonia and Achaia and go to Jerusalem , saying , " After I have been there I must see Rome also . "
44019022	He sent on into Macedonia two of his assistants , Timothy and Erastus , but he himself remained awhile in Asia .
44019023	At that time there arose no small commotion about the Way .
44019024	For a certain man named Demetrius , a silversmith , a maker of silver shrines of Artemis , was bringing to the artisans no small gain .
44019025	He gathered these and the workmen employed about such things and said , " Men , you know that from this business we get our wealth ,
44019026	and you see and hear that not only at Ephesus , but also throughout almost all Asia this Paul has persuaded and drawn away a large number , saying that hand-made gods are not gods at all .
44019027	Not only is this trade of ours in danger of coming into disrepute , but also the temple of the great goddess Artemis is in danger of being held of no account , and she whom now all Asia and the wide world worship will be deposed from her majesty . "
44019028	Upon hearing this , they became full of anger and shouted , " Great is Artemis of the Ephesians ! "
44019029	The city was filled with confusion , and the people rushed with one mind into the theater , having gotten hold of Gaius and Aristarchus , fellow travelers of Paul's .
44019030	When Paul wished to go in and face the people the disciples would not let him .
44019031	Some of the city officials who were his friends sent to him and begged him not to expose himself in the theater .
44019032	Some were shouting one thing and some another , for the assembly was in confusion , and the most did not know why they had come together .
44019033	Some of the crowd fixed on Alexander , since the Jews were putting him forward . And Alexander motioned with his hand and wished to make a defense before the people .
44019034	But when they recognized that he was a Jew , there arose one shout from all for about two hours , " Great is Artemis of the Ephesians ! "
44019035	Then the City Clerk quieted the crowd and said , " Men of Ephesus , who is there of all men who does not know that the city of Ephesus is the temple-keeper of the great Artemis , and of her image which fell down from Zeus ?
44019036	Since these things are indisputable , you ought to be calm and do nothing rash .
44019037	For you have brought here these men who are not robbers of temples nor defamers of your goddess .
44019038	If Demetrius and the artisans with him have a charge against any one , there are court days and there are proconsuls ; let the parties state their cases .
44019039	If you are seeking anything further , it shall be settled in a lawful assembly .
44019040	For we are in danger of being called in question regarding to-day's mob , and we shall not be able to give a reason for this tumult . "
44019041	By saying this he dissolved the gathering .
44020001	WHEN the uproar had ceased , Paul sent for the disciples , and , after encouraging them , he bade them farewell and left to proceed to Macedonia .
44020002	Passing through those parts and encouraging them by many addresses , he came into Greece .
44020003	There he spent three months . When a plot was formed against him by the Jews as he was about to sail for Syria , he decided to return through Macedonia .
44020004	There were in company with him Sopater of Beraea , the son of Pyrrhus , and of the Thessalonians Aristarchus and Secundus , and Gaius of Derbe and Timothy , and from Asia Tychicus and Trophimus .
44020005	These went on and were waiting for us in Troas .
44020006	After the Days of Unleavened Bread we sailed from Philippi and came to them in Troas in five days . There we spent seven days .
44020007	On the first day of the week , when we all were assembled to break bread , Paul was discoursing to them , being about to leave in the morning , and he extended his address until midnight .
44020008	There were many lamps in the upper room where we were assembled .
44020009	A certain young man named Eutychus , sitting in a window , was overcome with deep sleep while Paul went on discoursing . At last overpowered by sleep he fell from the third story and was taken up dead .
44020010	But Paul went down and threw himself on him and embraced him and said , " Do not make a noisy wailing ; for his life is still in him . "
44020011	Then he went up and broke bread and ate and talked on till daybreak and so departed .
44020012	They brought the boy living , and were not a little comforted .
44020013	We went in advance to the ship and sailed for Assos , intending to take on Paul there , for so he had arranged , intending to come himself by land .
44020014	So when he joined us at Assos , we took him aboard and came to Mitylene .
44020015	From there we sailed next day and arrived off Chios . The next day we came to Samos , and on the following day to Miletus .
44020016	For Paul had determined to sail by Ephesus in order not to spend time in Asia . He was hurrying to be in Jerusalem , if possible , on the Day of Pentecost .
44020017	From Miletus he sent to Ephesus for the elders of the church .
44020018	When they came to him , he said to them , " You know how I have lived among you the whole time since the first day I set foot in Asia ,
44020019	serving the Lord with all humility and with tears and with trials that befell me through the plots of the Jews â
44020020	how I did not shrink from telling you anything that was profitable or from teaching you publicly and from house to house ,
44020021	urging upon both Jews and Greeks the need of a change of heart toward God and of faith in our Lord Jesus .
44020022	" And now I am on my way , bound in spirit , to Jerusalem , not knowing what is to befall me there ,
44020023	except that the Holy Spirit testifies from city to city that chains and trials are waiting for me .
44020024	But I do not hold my life as of any account if only I may finish my race and the service which I received from the Lord Jesus , to testify to the good news of the grace of God .
44020025	And now I know that you all , among whom I have gone about heralding the kingdom , will never see my face again .
44020026	Therefore I testify to you to-day that I am clear of the blood of all .
44020027	For I did not shrink from telling you the whole purpose of God .
44020028	" Be watchful of yourselves and of all the flock of which the Holy Spirit has placed you as overseers . Shepherd the church of God which he bought with his own blood .
44020029	I know that after my departure fierce wolves will come among you , not sparing the flock .
44020030	And from among yourselves men will arise speaking perverse things to draw away the disciples after themselves .
44020031	Therefore watch , remembering that for three years I never ceased night nor day to exhort each one of you with tears .
44020032	" And now I commit you to the Lord and to his gracious message , which can build you up and give you the heritage among all those who have been made holy .
44020033	I have coveted no man's silver or gold or apparel .
44020034	You yourselves know that these hands provided for my needs and the needs of my companions .
44020035	In all things I showed you that so laboring we ought to help the weak , and to remember the words of the Lord Jesus , that he said , ' It is more blessed to give than to receive . '
44020036	After saying this he kneeled with them all and prayed .
44020037	All wept aloud , and falling on Paul's neck they kissed him affectionately ,
44020038	grieving especially because he had said that they would never see his face again ; and they escorted him to the ship .
44021001	WHEN we had torn ourselves away from them and had sailed , we made a straight run to Cos , then on the next day to Rhodes and from there to Patara .
44021002	There finding a ship crossing to Phoenicia we went on board and sailed .
44021003	After sighting Cyprus and leaving it on the left , we sailed on to Syria and landed at Tyre ; for there the ship was to discharge her cargo .
44021004	We looked up the disciples and stayed with them seven days . They repeatedly told Paul through the Holy Spirit not to go up to Jerusalem .
44021005	But when we had finished the days , we left and continued our journey , and they all with their wives and children escorted us until we got outside of the city . Then , after kneeling down on the beach and praying ,
44021006	we tore ourselves from one another ; we went aboard the ship and they went back to their homes .
44021007	We made the voyage from Tyre and arrived at Ptolemais . There we greeted the brethren and remained one day with them .
44021008	On the next day we left and came to Caesarea , and entered the house of Philip the evangelist , who was one of the Seven , and we stayed with him .
44021009	Philip had four unmarried daughters who had the gift of prophecy .
44021010	During our stay of many days a certain prophet named Agabus came down from Jerusalem .
44021011	He came to see us , and took Paul's belt and bound his own feet and hands and said , " Thus says the Holy Spirit , ' So will the Jews in Jerusalem bind the man who owns this belt , and will deliver him into the hands of the Gentiles . ' "
44021012	When we heard this , both we and the residents there begged him not to go up to Jerusalem .
44021013	Paul answered , " What are you accomplishing by weeping and breaking my heart ? For I hold myself ready not only to be bound , but to die in Jerusalem for the name of the Lord Jesus . "
44021014	When he would not be persuaded , we stopped talking , saying , " The Lord's will be done . "
44021015	At the end of these days we packed up and went up to Jerusalem .
44021016	Some of the disciples from Caesarea went up with us , taking along Mnason , a Cypriote , an old-time disciple , whose guests we were to be .
44021017	When we reached Jerusalem , the brethren welcomed us cordially .
44021018	On the next day , Paul went in with us for an interview with James , and all the elders came .
44021019	After saluting them , he related in detail all that God had done among the Gentiles through his service .
44021020	After hearing him , they gave glory to God and said to Paul , " You see , brother , how many tens of thousands of believers there are among the Jews , and they are all zealous for the Law .
44021021	These have heard reports that you are teaching all the Jews who live among the Gentiles to break away from Moses , telling them not to circumcise their children and not to observe the customs .
44021022	What then ? It will be generally heard that you have come .
44021023	So do this that we tell you . There are among us four men who are under a vow .
44021024	Take these men and go through purification with them and pay their expenses , so that they may shave their heads . Then all will know that what they have heard about you amounts to nothing , but that you yourself walk in obedience to the Law .
44021025	" But as to the Gentiles that have believed , we have , after consideration , sent our decision that they shall guard themselves against what has been sacrificed to idols , and against blood , and against what has been strangled , and against unchastity . "
44021026	Then Paul on the next day took the men , and , after purifying himself , entered the Temple courts , giving notice of the completion of the days of purification â the time until a sacrifice would have been offered for each one of them .
44021027	But when the seven days were nearly completed , the Jews from Asia saw him in the Temple courts , and stirred up all the crowd and laid their hands on Paul ,
44021028	shouting , " Men of Israel , help . This is the man who teaches everybody everywhere against our people and the Law and this place , and moreover , he has brought Greeks into the Temple courts and has desecrated this holy place . "
44021029	For they had previously seen Trophimus the Ephesian in the city with Paul , and they thought that he had brought him into the Temple courts .
44021030	The whole city was excited and the people rushed together . Seizing Paul , they drew him out of the Temple courts , and immediately the gates were closed .
44021031	As they were trying to kill him , word went up to the Tribune of the battalion that all Jerusalem was in commotion .
44021032	He at once took soldiers and centurions and ran down to the people . They , on seeing the Tribune and the soldiers , stopped beating Paul .
44021033	Then the Tribune coming up arrested him and ordered him to be bound with two chains , and inquired who he was and what he had done .
44021034	Some called out one thing and some another in the crowd . Not being able to find out anything for certain on account of the confusion , he ordered Paul to be taken into the barracks .
44021035	When Paul got upon the stairs , it so happened that he was being carried by the soldiers on account of the violence of the mob .
44021036	For the crowd of people was following and shouting , " Kill him ! "
44021037	As he was about to enter the barracks Paul said to the Tribune , " May I say something to you ? " He replied , " Can you speak Greek ?
44021038	Are you then not the Egyptian who some time ago raised a sedition and led off four thousand assassins into the desert ? "
44021039	Paul said , " I am a Jew from Tarsus , in Cilicia , a citizen of no insignificant city . I beg you to let me talk to the people . "
44021040	He gave him leave , and Paul standing on the stairs motioned with his hand to the people . There was a great silence , and , speaking loudly in Hebrew , Paul said :
44022001	" BRETHREN and Fathers , listen to the defense I now make to you . "
44022002	Hearing him speaking to them in the Hebrew language , they kept all the more quiet . He continued :
44022003	" I am a Jew , born in Tarsus , in Cilicia , but brought up in this city , educated at the feet of Gamaliel in exact knowledge of our ancestral Law , and I was zealous for God as you all are to-day .
44022004	I persecuted this Way to the death , binding and delivering into prison both men and women ,
44022005	as the High Priest and all the eldership can testify for me . From them I received letters to the brethren and was journeying to Damascus in order to bring back in chains to Jerusalem for punishment those who had gone there .
44022006	It happened that as I was journeying and nearing Damascus , about noon , suddenly a great light flashed from heaven around me .
44022007	I fell to the ground and heard a voice saying to me , ' Saul , Saul , why are you persecuting me ? '
44022008	I asked , ' Who is speaking ? ' He said to me , ' I am Jesus the Nazarene , whom you are persecuting . '
44022009	My companions saw the light , but did not hear the voice of him who spoke to me .
44022010	I said , ' What shall I do , Lord ? ' The Lord said to me , ' Rise and go into Damascus , and there you will be told about all that it has been appointed for you to do . '
44022011	Since I could not see , owing to the brightness of that light , my companions led me by the hand , and so I entered Damascus .
44022012	" Then a man named Ananias , a strict observer of the Law and highly esteemed by all the Jews who lived there ,
44022013	came to see me and stood by me and said , ' Brother Saul , receive your sight , ' and I , at that moment , could see him .
44022014	He said , ' The God of our fathers has appointed you to know his will , and to see the Righteous One and to hear the voice from his mouth ,
44022015	for you shall be a witness for him to all men of what you have seen and heard .
44022016	And now why delay ? Rise , be baptized and wash away your sins , calling upon his name . '
44022017	" After I had returned to Jerusalem , and was praying in the Temple courts , I fell into a trance
44022018	and saw Jesus saying to me , ' Hasten and depart quickly from Jerusalem , for they will not receive your testimony concerning me . '
44022019	But I said , ' Lord , they know that I used to imprison and beat from synagogue to synagogue those who believe in thee ,
44022020	and when the blood of Stephen thy martyr was shed I myself was standing by and approving it , and taking care of the cloaks of those who were putting him to death . '
44022021	But he said to me , ' Go , for I will send you far away to Gentiles . '
44022022	They listened up to this point , but now they broke out , shouting , " Away with such a fellow from the earth ! He ought never to have lived ! "
44022023	While they were shouting and rending their garments and throwing dust into the air ,
44022024	the Tribune ordered him to be led into the barracks and directed that he should be examined with the lash , so that he might know for what crime they were shouting so against him .
44022025	When they had tied him up with the thongs , Paul said to the Centurion who was standing by , " Is it lawful for you to scourge a man who is a Roman , and without a trial ? "
44022026	On hearing that , the Centurion went to the Tribune and told him , " What are you going to do ? For this man is a Roman . "
44022027	Then the Tribune came to him and said , " Tell me ; are you a Roman ? " He said , " Yes . "
44022028	The Tribune said , " I obtained this citizenship by paying a great sum of money . " Paul said , " But I was born to it . "
44022029	At once those who were about to examine him went away from him , and the Tribune was alarmed when he learned that he was a Roman , because he had chained him .
44022030	On the next day , wishing to know certainly why he was accused by the Jews , the Tribune loosed Paul and ordered the high priests and all the Council to assemble , and brought Paul down and stood him before them .
44023001	PAUL fixed his eyes on the Council and said , " Brethren , I have conducted myself with all good conscience toward God up to this day . "
44023002	The High Priest Ananias told those who stood near him to strike him on the mouth .
44023003	Then Paul said to him , " God will soon strike you , you whitewashed wall . Are you sitting to judge me by the Law and yet violating the Law by ordering me to be struck ? "
44023004	Those who stood by said , " Are you insulting God's High Priest ? "
44023005	Paul said , " I did not know , brethren , that he was High Priest . It is written , ' Thou shalt not speak evil of the Ruler of thy people . ' "
44023006	Then Paul , perceiving that one party was of Sadducees and the other of Pharisees , shouted out in the Council , " Brethren , I am a Pharisee , a son of Pharisees . I am being tried for the hope of the resurrection of the dead . "
44023007	On his saying this , a dissension arose between the Pharisees and Sadducees , and the assembly became divided .
44023008	For the Sadducees say that there is no resurrection nor any angel or spirit , but the Pharisees confess both .
44023009	So a great uproar arose , and some of the scribes of the party of the Pharisees arose and contended , saying , " We find nothing wrong in this man . What if a spirit has spoken to him , or an angel ? "
44023010	When the strife was becoming violent , the Tribune , fearing that Paul might be torn to pieces by them , ordered the soldiers to go down and take him from the midst of them and bring him into the barracks .
44023011	On the following night the Lord stood beside Paul and said , " Courage ! As you have witnessed for me in Jerusalem , so you must witness in Rome . "
44023012	When it was day , the Jews made a conspiracy and bound themselves by an oath not to eat or drink until they had killed Paul .
44023013	There were more than forty who had taken this oath .
44023014	They came to the high priests and elders and said , " We have bound ourselves by an oath to taste nothing until we have killed Paul .
44023015	Now therefore you and the Council must ask the Tribune to bring him down to you , as if you were going to inquire more exactly about him , and we , before he comes near , will be ready to put him out of the way . "
44023016	But the son of Paul's sister heard of the ambush , and he came and entered the barracks and told Paul .
44023017	Paul called to him one of the centurions and said , " Take this young man to the Tribune , for he has something to tell him . "
44023018	He took him and led him to the Tribune and said , " Paul , the prisoner , called me and asked me to bring this young man to you . He has something to say to you . "
44023019	The Tribune took him by the hand and led him aside and asked , " What is it that you have to tell me ? "
44023020	He said , " The Jews have agreed to ask you to bring Paul down to-morrow to the Council to inquire something more exactly about him .
44023021	But do not yield to them , for more than forty men of them are lying in ambush , and they have taken an oath not to eat or drink until they have killed him , and now they are ready , expecting a promise from you . "
44023022	The Tribune dismissed the young man after charging him ; " Tell no one that you have revealed this to me . "
44023023	Then calling to him two of the centurions he said , " Prepare two hundred soldiers to go to Caesarea , and seventy horsemen and two hundred spearmen , at nine o'clock to-night . "
44023024	They were to provide animals for Paul to ride and take him safely to Felix the Governor .
44023025	He wrote a letter in the following form :
44023026	" Claudius Lysias to his Excellency , Governor Felix : greeting .
44023027	This man was seized by the Jews and was about to be killed by them when I came up with soldiers and rescued him , having learned that he was a Roman .
44023028	Wishing to find what was the charge that they had against him I took him down to their Council .
44023029	I found him accused regarding disputed questions of their law , but of nothing deserving of death or of bonds .
44023030	Information has come to me that there will be a plot against the man , and so I am sending him at once to you , and I have commanded his accusers to state their case against him before you . "
44023031	So the soldiers , according to their orders , took Paul and conducted him by night to Antipatris .
44023032	On the next day they let the horsemen go on with him , but they themselves returned to the barracks .
44023033	The horsemen came on to Caesarea and delivered the letter to the Governor , and also placed Paul before him .
44023034	He read the letter and asked of what province he was , and learned that he was from Cilicia .
44023035	Then he said , " I will hear what you have to say when your accusers also arrive . " He gave orders that Paul should be guarded in Herod's castle .
44024001	AFTER five days the High Priest Ananias came down with certain elders and an advocate named Tertullus , and they spoke against Paul to the Governor .
44024002	When Paul had been called in , Tertullus began to accuse him , saying , " Because we enjoy great peace through your administration and reforms are taking place for this nation through your prudence ,
44024003	we accept it always and everywhere , most excellent Felix , with all gratitude .
44024004	But not to burden you further , I beg you in your fairness to hear us briefly .
44024005	We have found this man a pest and an inciter of sedition among all the Jews throughout the world , and a leader of the sect of the Nazarenes .
44024006	He even tried to desecrate the Temple courts , but we overpowered him .
44024008	You yourself can examine him and learn from him as to all these things of which we are accusing him . "
44024009	The Jews joined in the attack upon him , affirming that these things were so .
44024010	Paul answered , when the Governor nodded to him to speak , " Because I know that for many years you have been a judge to this nation , I feel courage in defending myself .
44024011	You can ascertain that it is not more than twelve days since I went up to Jerusalem to worship .
44024012	Neither did they find me discussing with any one in the Temple courts nor making any tumultuous gatherings in the synagogues nor anywhere in the city ,
44024013	nor can they bring you proofs of their accusations against me .
44024014	" This I do confess to you , that in the Way which they call a heresy I worship the God of our fathers , believing all things that are according to the Law and what is written in the Prophets
44024015	and having the hope in God which they themselves also accept â that there will be a resurrection both of the just and of the unjust .
44024016	And in this I take pains , to have always a clear conscience toward God and toward men .
44024017	" After many years I came to my nation to make gifts of charity and offerings .
44024018	They found me in the Temple thus occupied and purified , with no crowd or noise â but there were some Jews from Asia ,
44024019	who ought to have been here before you to present their accusations if they had anything against me ,
44024020	or let these themselves say what wrong they found in me when I stood before the Council ;
44024021	unless it was in the single assertion that I shouted as I stood among them , ' It is regarding the resurrection of the dead that I am on trial to-day before you ! ' "
44024022	Felix adjourned the case , since he was well informed regarding the Way , saying , " When Lysias the Tribune comes down , I will inquire into your matters . "
44024023	He gave orders to the Centurion to guard him , but to let him have indulgence , and not to hinder any of his friends from attending to his wants .
44024024	After some days Felix came with Drusilla his wife , who was a Jewess , and sent for Paul and heard him regarding faith in Christ Jesus .
44024025	While Paul was reasoning about righteousness and self-discipline and the judgment that is to come , Felix became alarmed and said , " Go for the present . When I find a convenient time I will send for you . "
44024026	At the same time he was in hopes that money would be given him by Paul and therefore he used to send for him more frequently and converse with him .
44024027	But at the end of two years Felix received Porcius Festus as a successor , and , wishing to do the Jews a favor , he left Paul in chains .
44025001	FESTUS entered the province and after three days went up to Jerusalem from Caesarea .
44025002	There the high priests and the leaders of the Jews spoke to him against Paul
44025003	and begged as a favor that he would send for him to Jerusalem , intending to have an ambush and kill him on the road .
44025004	But Festus answered that Paul was being kept in Caesarea and that he himself was going back very soon .
44025005	" Let those of you who can , " he said , " go down with me , and , if there is anything wrong about the man , let them bring their charges against him . "
44025006	After spending not more than eight or ten days among them , he went down to Caesarea and on the next day took his seat on the judge's bench and ordered Paul to be brought in .
44025007	When he had come in , the Jews who had come down from Jerusalem stood around him and brought many serious charges , which they were unable to prove ,
44025008	while Paul claimed in his own defense , " Neither against the Jewish Law nor against the Temple courts nor against Caesar , have I committed any wrong . "
44025009	Festus , wishing to gain favor with the Jews , asked Paul , " Are you willing to go up to Jerusalem and there be tried for this before me ? "
44025010	Paul said , " I am standing before Caesar's bar , where I ought to be tried . I have not harmed any Jews in anything , as you very well know .
44025011	If I am in the wrong and have committed anything worthy of death , I do not ask not to die . But if there is nothing in the accusations of these men , no one has the power to give me up to them . I appeal to Caesar . "
44025012	Then Festus , after talking with his council , answered , " You have appealed to Caesar ; to Caesar you shall go . "
44025013	When some days had passed , Agrippa the King and Bernice came to Caesarea to pay their respects to Festus .
44025014	As they were spending a good many days there , Festus laid Paul's case before the King . " There is a man here , " he said , " who was left a prisoner by Felix ,
44025015	against whom when I was in Jerusalem the high priests and the elders of the Jews had much to say , asking to have him condemned .
44025016	I answered them that it is not the custom of the Romans to give up any person for punishment before the accused has his accusers face to face and has opportunity for defense against the charge .
44025017	" So they came along down here and , without making any delay , on the very next day I took my seat on the judge's bench and ordered the man to be brought in .
44025018	When his accusers arose , they brought no charge of such crimes as I was expecting ,
44025019	but they had some disputes with him about their own religion and concerning a certain Jesus who had died and whom Paul affirmed to be alive .
44025020	Being at a loss about a question of this kind , I asked if he would be willing to go to Jerusalem and be tried there on the charges .
44025021	But when Paul appealed to be kept for the examination of the Emperor , I ordered him to be kept until I could send him to Caesar . "
44025022	Agrippa said to Festus , " I should like to hear the man myself . " " To-morrow , " he replied , " you shall hear him . "
44025023	So on the next day Agrippa came and Bernice with much display , and they entered the auditorium with the military tribunes and the principal men of the city , and at Festus ' command Paul was led in .
44025024	Festus said , " King Agrippa and all present here with us , you see this man against whom all the multitude of the Jews pleaded with me , both in Jerusalem and here , crying out that he ought not to live any longer .
44025025	But I understood that he had done nothing worthy of death , and when he himself had appealed to the Emperor , I decided to send him .
44025026	Concerning him I have nothing certain to write to my Lord . Therefore I have brought him before you all , and especially before you , King Agrippa , that after an examination I may have something to write .
44025027	For it seems to me unreasonable in sending a prisoner not to specify the charges against him . "
44026001	AGRIPPA said to Paul , " You are at liberty to speak for yourself . " Then Paul stretched out his hand and made his defense :
44026002	" In regard to all of the things of which I am accused by Jews , King Agrippa , I consider myself fortunate that I am to make my defense to-day before you ,
44026003	since you are especially expert in all Jewish customs and questions . Therefore I pray you to hear me patiently .
44026004	" My life from boyhood , which was from the beginning among my own nation and in Jerusalem , all Jews know .
44026005	They knew me from long ago , if they were willing to testify , and that according to the strictest sect of our religion I lived a Pharisee .
44026006	And now I stand to be tried for the hope of the promise which God made to our fathers ,
44026007	to which our twelve tribes devotedly serving God night and day hope to attain . For this hope I am accused by the Jews , O King .
44026008	" Why do all of you consider it incredible if God raises dead men ?
44026009	I thought with myself that I ought to do much against the name of Jesus the Nazarene .
44026010	And I did it in Jerusalem and many holy men I shut up in prison , getting authority from the high priests , and when they were put to death I gave my vote against them .
44026011	In all the synagogues and often I punished them and compelled them to say profane words . Being excessively mad against them , I pursued them even to foreign cities .
44026012	" Thus engaged , as I was journeying to Damascus with authority and commission from the high priests ,
44026013	about midday , on the road , I saw , O King , a light above the brightness of the sun shining from heaven around me and my companions .
44026014	We all fell to the ground and I heard a voice saying to me in Hebrew , ' Saul , Saul , why are you persecuting me ? It is hard for you to kick against the goad . '
44026015	I said , ' Who is speaking ? ' He said , ' I am Jesus whom you are persecuting .
44026016	But rise and stand on your feet : for I have appeared to you for the very purpose of appointing you a servant and a witness of the times you have seen me and of the times I shall appear to you .
44026017	I will deliver you from your people and from the Gentiles , to whom I am sending you ,
44026018	to open their eyes and turn them from darkness to light and from the power of Satan to God , that they may receive forgiveness of sins and inheritance among those who are made holy by faith in me . '
44026019	After that , King Agrippa , I was not disobedient to the heavenly vision ,
44026020	but first to the people in Damascus and then to the people of Jerusalem and through all the land of Judaea and to the Gentiles , I proclaimed that they should repent and turn to God and do deeds suitable for a change of heart .
44026021	" For this reason Jews seized me in the Temple courts and tried to kill me .
44026022	But obtaining help from God I have continued until this day witnessing to small and great , saying nothing but what the prophets and Moses said would be ,
44026023	that the Christ would suffer and that he first , by rising from the dead , would proclaim light to our people and to the Gentiles . "
44026024	While Paul was thus defending himself , Festus said loudly , " You are raving , Paul . Much learning is driving you insane . "
44026025	" I am not insane , " he said , " most noble Festus , but am uttering words of truth and soberness .
44026026	The King knows about this , and to him I speak with perfect frankness , for I am persuaded that not one of these things has escaped his attention , for this has not been done in a corner .
44026027	King Agrippa , do you believe the prophets ? I know that you believe them . "
44026028	Agrippa said to Paul , " With little effort you are persuading me to become a Christian . "
44026029	Paul said , " I would to God that whether with little or with much , not only you , but all who hear me this day , would become such as I am â except for these chains . "
44026030	Then the King rose and the Governor and Bernice and those who had been sitting with them ,
44026031	and after withdrawing they said to one another , " This man is doing nothing deserving of death or chains . "
44026032	Agrippa said to Festus , " This man could have been set at liberty if he had not appealed to Caesar . "
44027001	WHEN it was decided that we should sail for Italy , they committed Paul and certain other prisoners to a centurion named Julius , of an imperial battalion .
44027002	Going on board a ship of Adramyttium which was about to sail to the places along the coast of Asia we put to sea . Aristarchus , a Macedonian of Thessalonica , was with us .
44027003	On the next day we reached Sidon , where Julius treated Paul kindly and allowed him to go to see his friends and enjoy their attentions .
44027004	Putting to sea from there , we sailed under the lee of Cyprus because the winds were contrary .
44027005	After crossing the sea off Cilicia and Pamphylia , we came to Myra in Lycia .
44027006	There the centurion found an Alexandrian ship bound for Italy and put us on board of her .
44027007	By slow sailing for many days we with difficulty arrived off Cnidus . Then the wind being against us , we sailed under the lee of Crete off Salmone
44027008	and with difficulty got past it and came to a place called Fair Havens , near which was the city of Lasea .
44027009	When much time had passed and sailing was now dangerous because it was already after the Fast , Paul addressed them .
44027010	" Men , " he said , " I see that the voyage is going to be rough and with much loss not only of the cargo and the ship but also of our lives . "
44027011	But the Centurion listened more to the sailing master and the ship owner than to what Paul said ,
44027012	and as the harbor was not convenient to winter in , the majority adopted the purpose of sailing away on the chance of being able to reach Phoenix and winter there . Phoenix is a harbor of Crete facing the southwest and the northwest .
44027013	When the south wind blew softly , thinking that they had secured their purpose , they weighed anchor and coasted along Crete .
44027014	But before long a hurricane , such as is called Euraquilo , swept down off the land .
44027015	When the ship was caught and unable to keep her head to the wind , we gave up and let her drive before it .
44027016	Running under the lee of an island called Cauda , we contrived with difficulty to secure the small boat .
44027017	When we had got it in , we used ropes to undergird the ship . Fearing that we might get stranded on the Syrtis , they lowered the sail and so drifted .
44027018	So violently were we battered by the storm that on the next day they lightened the ship
44027019	and on the third day with their own hands they threw over the ship's tackle .
44027020	When for many days neither sun nor stars appeared and no small tempest lay on us , at last all hope of our being saved was being taken away .
44027021	After they had long gone without food , Paul stood up in the midst of them and said , " Men , you ought to have listened to me and not to have sailed away from Crete and met this rough experience and loss .
44027022	But now I beg you to have courage , for there will be no loss of life of any of you , but only of the ship .
44027023	For this night an angel of the God whose I am and whom I serve stood by me
44027024	and said , ' Never fear , Paul ! You must stand before Caesar . And now God has granted to you all the men who are sailing with you . '
44027025	So cheer up , men . For I trust in God that it will be as it has been told me .
44027026	We must , however , run on to a certain island . "
44027027	When the fourteenth night came , as we were being driven through the Adriatic , about midnight the sailors surmised that land was getting near .
44027028	Sounding they found twenty fathoms , and after a little they sounded again and found fifteen fathoms .
44027029	Then fearing that they might run into rocky places , they cast out four anchors from the stern and prayed for day to come .
44027030	The sailors were intent on escaping from the ship and lowered the small boat into the sea under the pretense of laying out anchors from the bow ,
44027031	but Paul said to the Centurion and the soldiers , " Unless these men stay in the ship , you cannot be saved . "
44027032	Then the soldiers cut the ropes of the small boat and let her fall off .
44027033	Until day began to dawn , Paul kept urging all to take food . He said , " To-day is the fourteenth day that you have been on the watch fasting , not taking anything .
44027034	Therefore , I beg you , take some food . For this is for your safety . Not a hair of the head of any one of you is going to perish . "
44027035	Saying this he took a loaf and gave thanks to God before all and broke it and began to eat .
44027036	Then all cheered up and themselves took food .
44027037	We in the ship were in all two hundred and seventy-six souls .
44027038	After eating heartily , they lightened the ship , throwing over the wheat into the sea .
44027039	When day came they did not recognize the land , but they observed a bay with a beach . Into this they planned to run the ship if they could .
44027040	So abandoning the anchors they left them in the sea ; at the same time loosening the bands of the steering oars and raising the foresail to the wind , they made for the beach .
44027041	But falling into a place where there were cross-currents they ran the ship aground . The bow stuck fast and remained immovable , but the stern was breaking up under the violence of the sea .
44027042	The soldiers ' advice was to kill the prisoners for fear that some one of them might swim out and escape .
44027043	But the Centurion , wishing to save Paul , kept them back from their plan . He ordered those who could swim to jump overboard first and get to shore ,
44027044	and the rest to follow , some on boards and some on things from the ship . And so all got safe to land .
44028001	WHEN we were safe ashore , we found that the island was called Melita .
44028002	The foreign people showed us uncommon kindness . For they kindled a fire and welcomed us all because of the rain that was falling and the cold .
44028003	Paul had collected a bundle of sticks and laid it on the fire , when a snake came out of the heat and fastened on his hand .
44028004	When the foreigners saw the creature hanging from his hand , they said to one another , " Certainly this man is a murderer , whom , although he has escaped the sea , Justice does not permit to live . "
44028005	He however shook off the creature into the fire and felt no harm .
44028006	They kept watching to see him swell up or suddenly fall down dead . But after watching a long time and seeing nothing amiss happen to him , they changed their minds and said that he was a god .
44028007	In the neighborhood of that place were lands belonging to the Governor of the island , whose name was Publius . He welcomed us and for three days hospitably entertained us .
44028008	It happened that the father of Publius was lying ill with fever and dysentery . Paul went in to see him and prayed and laid his hands on him and healed him .
44028009	After this happened , the rest in the island who had infirmities came also and were healed .
44028010	They bestowed many honors on us and when we sailed they put on board supplies for our needs .
44028011	After three months we sailed in a ship that had wintered in the island . She was from Alexandria and her figure-head was the Twin Brothers .
44028012	Landing at Syracuse we remained there three days .
44028013	From there we came around and got to Rhegium . After one day there , a south wind sprang up and we came on the second day to Puteoli .
44028014	Here we found brethren and were begged by them to stay seven days . And so we came to Rome .
44028015	From there the brethren , when they got news of us , came to meet us as far as the Market of Appius and the Three Taverns . On seeing them Paul thanked God and took courage .
44028016	When we reached Rome , Paul was allowed to live by himself with a soldier who guarded him .
44028017	After three days he invited the leading men among the Jews , and when they had assembled , he said to them , " Brethren , although I had done nothing against our people or our ancestral customs , I was delivered up as a prisoner from Jerusalem into the hands of the Romans .
44028018	They , after investigating my case , wished to set me free because I had done nothing deserving of death .
44028019	But when the Jews spoke against it , I was compelled to appeal to Caesar , not that I have any charge to bring against my own nation .
44028020	For this reason I have invited you to see me and talk with me ; because it is for the sake of the hope of Israel that I have this chain around me . "
44028021	They said to him , " We on our part have received no letters about you from Judaea nor has any one of the brethren come and reported or spoken anything evil of you .
44028022	We think it well to hear from you what your views are ; for as to this sect we know that it is everywhere spoken against . "
44028023	They appointed a day for him and many came to him at his lodging . He explained to them , testifying to the kingdom of God , trying to persuade them concerning Jesus from the Law of Moses and from the Prophets , from early morning until evening .
44028024	Some were persuaded by what he said and some did not believe .
44028025	They dispersed , disagreeing with one another , after Paul had said one word , " Well said the Holy Spirit through Isaiah , the prophet , to your fathers ,
44028026	' Go to this people and say , You will hear plainly but you will not understand , and you will see plainly but you will not perceive .
44028027	For the heart of this people has grown fat and with their ears they are hard of hearing and their eyes they have shut , so that they may never see with their eyes nor hear with their ears nor understand with their heart and repent , so that I may heal them . '
44028028	Therefore be it known to you that this salvation of God has been sent to the Gentiles . They will listen . "
44028030	Paul remained two whole years in his own rented lodging and received all who came to him ,
44028031	proclaiming the kingdom of God and teaching about the Lord Jesus Christ with all freedom of speech , unhindered .
45001001	PAUL , a servant of Christ Jesus , called to be an apostle , set apart to bear the good news of God ,
45001002	which he foretold through his prophets in Holy Scripture ,
45001003	concerning his Son Jesus Christ our Lord ( who became one of the descendants of David according to the flesh ,
45001004	and was with power proved to be the Son of God according to the Spirit of holiness by his resurrection from the dead ) ;
45001005	through whom we obtained grace and apostleship to promote obedience of faith for the sake of his name ,
45001006	among all the Gentiles , among whom are you , called by Jesus Christ ;
45001007	to all who are in Rome , beloved by God , called to be holy : Grace to you and peace from God our Father and the Lord Jesus Christ .
45001008	First of all I thank my God through Jesus Christ for all of you , because your faith is spoken of through all the world .
45001009	For God , whom I serve in my spirit in the good news of his Son , is my witness how unceasingly I make mention of you , always in my prayers
45001010	asking if I may somehow at some time by the will of God find the way open to come to you .
45001011	For I long to see you that I may impart to you some spiritual gift of grace in order that you may be strengthened ,
45001012	that is , that I may be encouraged with you and by you through our mutual faith , yours and mine .
45001013	I am not willing that you should be ignorant , brethren , that often I have purposed to come to you , in order that I might have some fruit among you as among the other Gentiles .
45001014	I am a debtor to Greeks and to Barbarians , to wise men and to unthinking men ;
45001015	so , for my part , I am eager to tell the good news also to you in Rome .
45001016	For I am not ashamed of the good news . It is the power of God for salvation to every one who believes , to the Jew first and also to the Greek .
45001017	For a righteousness of God is revealed in it from faith to faith , as it is written , " He who is righteous by faith shall live . "
45001018	For the wrath of God is revealed from heaven against all impiety and wickedness of men who hold the truth but practice unrighteousness .
45001019	Because what may be known of God is manifest within them , for God has manifested it to them .
45001020	For God's invisible qualities â his everlasting power and deity â are , since the creation of the world , clearly seen , being known from what he has made . So they are without any excuse .
45001021	For although they knew God they did not glorify him as God and did not give him thanks , but fell into futile speculations and their stupid hearts were darkened .
45001022	Boasting of being wise , they became fools
45001023	and changed the glory of the incorruptible God into images of mortal man , and of birds and beasts and reptiles .
45001024	Therefore God gave them over , in the lusts of their hearts , to uncleanness , to dishonor their bodies mutually .
45001025	They changed the truth of God into a lie , and reverenced and paid worship to the creature rather than to the Creator â who is blessed forever , Amen !
45001026	Therefore God gave them over to disgraceful passions . For their females changed the natural use for one contrary to nature ,
45001027	and their males , leaving the natural use of the female , burned in their lust for one another , males with males practicing indecency and receiving in themselves the deserved penalty of their error .
45001028	And as they did not think fit to keep God in their knowledge , God gave them over to an abandoned mind , to do the things that are shameful ,
45001029	filled with all injustice , wickedness , greed , malice , full of envy , murder , strife , fraud , malignant craftiness , whisperers ,
45001030	slanderers , hateful to God , insolent , arrogant , boasters , inventors of evil things , disobedient to parents ,
45001031	without common sense , without faithfulness , without family affection , without pity .
45001032	They know the just judgment of God that those who practice such things are worthy of death , yet they not only do them themselves , but are pleased with those who practice them .
45002001	THEREFORE you are without excuse , O man , whoever you are , when you judge . For in judging another you condemn yourself . For you , the judge , practice the same things .
45002002	But we know that the judgment of God is according to truth upon those who practice such things .
45002003	Do you think , O man , you who judge those who practice such things while you do the same , that you will escape the judgment of God ?
45002004	Or do you despise the wealth of his kindness and forbearance and long-suffering , not knowing that the kindness of God is calling you to a change of heart ?
45002005	Are you with a hard and unrepentant heart treasuring for yourself wrath for the day of wrath and for the revelation of the just judgment of God ?
45002006	He will give to each an award according to his works .
45002007	To those who by constancy in good work seek for glory and honor and immortality he will award life eternal .
45002008	But to those of a partisan spirit who do not obey the truth , but obey wickedness , there will be wrath and hot anger .
45002009	Distress and crushing calamity will fall upon every human soul that works evil , upon the Jew first and also upon the Greek .
45002010	But glory and honor and peace will come to every one who works good , to the Jew first and also to the Greek .
45002011	For God has no partiality .
45002012	As many as have sinned without a law will perish without a law , and as many as have sinned under law will be judged by law
45002013	( for it is not the hearers of law who are righteous before God , but the doers of law are pronounced righteous ;
45002014	for when Gentiles who have no law do by nature what the Law enjoins , these , although they have no law , are a law to themselves ;
45002015	they show the requirements of the Law written in their hearts , since their conscience corroborates it and their thoughts argue in mutual accusation or in self-defense ) ,
45002016	on the day when God judges the secrets of men through Jesus Christ , as my good news sets forth .
45002017	But if you bear the name of Jew and rely upon the Law , and make your boast in God
45002018	and know his will and are a judge of things that differ , because you have been taught out of the Law
45002019	and are confident that you yourself are a guide of the blind , a light of those who are in darkness ,
45002020	an instructor of the unwise , a teacher of the simple , because you have the form of knowledge and of truth in the Law â
45002021	you who are teaching another , do you not teach yourself ? You who preach not to steal , do you steal ?
45002022	You who say not to commit adultery , do you commit adultery ? You who abhor idols , do you rob temples ?
45002023	You who boast of the Law , do you dishonor God by breaking the Law ?
45002024	For " The name of God is reviled among the Gentiles because of you , " as it is written .
45002025	Circumcision has value if you obey the Law . But if you are a breaker of the Law , your circumcision has become uncircumcision .
45002026	If an uncircumcised man keeps the requirements of the Law , shall not his uncircumcision be credited for circumcision ?
45002027	And the natural uncircumcision if it keeps the Law will judge you who with a written code and circumcision are still a law-breaker .
45002028	For it is not he who is one outwardly that is a Jew , nor is that circumcision which is outward in the flesh .
45002029	But he who is one secretly is a Jew , and circumcision is of the heart and in the spirit , not in the letter . His praise is not from men , but from God .
45003001	WHAT then is the advantage of the Jew , or what is the benefit of circumcision ?
45003002	Much in every way . First , they were intrusted with the oracles of God .
45003003	For what if some were faithless , will their faithlessness prevent the faithfulness of God ?
45003004	Never . Let God be true , but every man a liar , as it is written , " That thou mayest be proved right in thy words and triumph when thou art judged . "
45003005	But if our unrighteousness shows the righteousness of God , what shall we say ? Is God unrighteous when he inflicts his wrath ?
45003006	Never . If so how can God judge the world ?
45003007	But if the truth of God has become more abundant to his glory through my lie , why am I still condemned as a sinner ?
45003008	We are not going to say , as some people slanderously affirm that we say , " Let us do evil that good may come , " are we ? The condemnation of such people is just .
45003009	What then ? Have we an advantage ? Not at all . We have already brought the charge against both Jews and Greeks that they are all under sin ,
45003010	as it is written , " There is not even one righteous ;
45003011	there is none that seeks God .
45003012	All have turned away ; together they have become worthless ; there is none who does what is useful , not even one .
45003013	Their throat is an open sepulcher ; with their tongues they deceive ; the poison of asps is under their lips .
45003014	Their mouth is full of cursing and bitterness ;
45003015	their feet are swift to shed blood ;
45003016	ruin and misery are in their paths .
45003017	The path of peace they do not know .
45003018	There is no reverence for God before their eyes . "
45003019	We know that all that the Law says , it says to those who are under the Law , that every mouth may be shut and all the world may come under the condemnation of God .
45003020	Therefore by works of the Law no human being will be pronounced righteous before him . For through the Law comes the knowledge of sin .
45003021	But now , apart from law , a righteousness of God has been revealed , confirmed by the Law and the Prophets â
45003022	a righteousness from God through faith in Jesus Christ for all believers . For there is no difference .
45003023	All have sinned and have come short of the glory of God .
45003024	All are pronounced righteous by his grace through the redemption that is in Christ Jesus ,
45003025	whom God has set forth as a propitiation by his blood through faith , for the manifestation of his righteousness , because of the passing over of previous sins in the forbearance of God â
45003026	for a manifestation at the present time of his righteousness , that he may himself be righteous and may accept as righteous him who has faith in Jesus .
45003027	Where then is boasting ? It is excluded . By what law ? That of works ? No , but by the law of faith .
45003028	For we reason that a man is pronounced righteous by faith aside from works of law .
45003029	Does God belong to the Jews only ? Does he not belong also to the Gentiles ? Yes , to the Gentiles ,
45003030	if God is one and will pronounce the circumcision righteous by faith and the uncircumcision righteous through faith .
45003031	Do we then by faith nullify the Law ? Never . On the contrary we establish the Law .
45004001	WHAT then shall we say that Abraham , our forefather according to the flesh , experienced ?
45004002	For if Abraham was pronounced righteous because of works , he had something to boast of . But he had nothing before God ;
45004003	for what says the Scripture ? " Abraham believed God , and it was credited to him for righteousness . "
45004004	To him who works , wages are credited not as by grace , but as due ;
45004005	but to him who does not work , but believes in him who calls the unrighteous man righteous , his faith is credited for righteousness .
45004006	Just so David speaks of the blessedness of the man to whom God credits righteousness apart from works ,
45004007	" Blessed are they whose lawless acts have been forgiven , and whose sins have been covered over .
45004008	Blessed is the man whose sin the Lord will not charge up to him . "
45004009	Does this blessedness come to the circumcision , or also to the uncircumcision ? For we say , " Faith was credited to Abraham for righteousness . "
45004010	How was it credited , when he was in circumcision or in uncircumcision ? Not in circumcision , but in uncircumcision .
45004011	And he received the sign of circumcision as a seal of the righteousness of faith that he had in uncircumcision , so that he should be the father of all who believe while uncircumcised , and righteousness should be credited to them ;
45004012	and the father of the circumcised , that is , of those who are not only circumcised , but who walk in the steps of the faith which our father Abraham had while uncircumcised .
45004013	It was not through the Law that the promise came to Abraham or to his descendants that he should be the heir of the world , but through the righteousness of faith .
45004014	For if those who are of the Law are heirs , faith is emptied of value and the promise is nullified .
45004015	For the Law works wrath . But where there is no law , neither is there lawbreaking .
45004016	Therefore all depends on faith , that it may be of grace , and thus the promise be sure for all his descendants , not only those who are of the Law , but also those who are of the faith of Abraham , who is the father of all of us
45004017	, in the view of the God whom he believed , who makes alive the dead and calls things that are not as if they were .
45004018	Abraham , when hope was past , believed in hope so that he became the father of many nations , according to what was said to him , " So shall your descendants be " ;
45004019	and without being weakened in faith he recognized his own body as dead , when he was about a hundred years old , and the deadness of Sarah's womb .
45004020	Still he did not hesitate through want of faith in the promise of God , but was strong in faith , thus giving glory to God ,
45004021	and was fully confident that what God had promised he was able to perform .
45004022	Therefore it was credited to him for righteousness .
45004023	It was not written for his sake only , that it was credited to him ,
45004024	but also for our sake , to whom it will be credited if we believe in him who raised up from the dead Jesus our Lord ,
45004025	who was delivered up on account of our sins and was raised again that we might be accounted righteous .
45005001	SO then , since we have been accounted righteous by faith , let us have peace with God , through our Lord Jesus Christ .
45005002	Through him we obtained entrance into this grace in which we stand and exult in hope of the glory of God .
45005003	Not only so , but we also exult in trials , knowing that trial develops endurance ,
